1. What did not get off the ground on July 8 in the O2 Arena in London?

2. Janine Krieber made one less friend on Facebook on Nov. 20. How?

3. What was unusual about the release of the Stephen King novella UR?

4.Preliminary searches in July were for court documents related to someone with the legal first name Bertram. By what name do Montrealers (and many Canadians) know him?

5.Which golfer came within a whisker of winning the British Open?

6. Of what economically wracked nation did Geir Hilmar Haarde cease to be prime minister on Feb. 1?

7.What m-word did Benoit Labonté use on Oct. 21?

8. There was no joy in Chicago, Madrid and Tokyo on Oct. 2. Why?

9.Which 75-year-old met which centenarian in the Bell Centre for a big show on April 2?

10.Birds were in the news on Jan. 15 after having caused what near-disaster?

11. Budd Schulberg, who died on Aug. 5, not only coulda been, he was the writer of what Academy-award-winning screenplay?

12. Eleven pirates attacked the Nivose in May. Why was this a bad move?

13.Who declared whose time to be up on Sept. 1?

14. What did Costa Rican president Oscar Arias come down with in July?

15. Why did the July G8 summit take place in the central Italian city of L'Aquila?

16. Which storied team started the season in a new stadium on April 16?

17. "... I would be remiss if I did not acknowledge the considerable controversy that your generous decision has generated." Who said this near the start of what acceptance speech?

18. CNN reported an earthquake in North Korea on May 24. How did the story develop?

19. Why did newscasters learn to pronounce Tegucigalpa on June 28?

20. It lasted six minutes and 39 seconds and probably had more people looking up than any other such occurrence in history. What?

21. Abdelbaset Ali Mohmed Al Megrahi arrived in Libya on August 20. From where?

22. What did Herman Van Rompuy become president of in November?

23. Cuba's loss is Illinois's gain. How?

24. The premiers of which two Canadian provinces signed a $4.8-billion deal on Oct. 29?

25. Which double-named anthropologist died on Oct. 30 at 100?

26. What pillar of talk television announced that 25 years would be enough?

27. Martin Cauchon or Nathalie Le Prohon. Which riding are we talking about?

28.Who sang a Lennon-McCartney favorite with the National Arts Centre Orchestra on Oct. 3?

29. Where did CityCenter open on Dec. 16?

30. "Apparently he was caught in a hotel room with a Schick Quattro." To whom was David Letterman referring with this punch line?

31. What could not be established as a cause of autism, according to the U.S. Court of Federal Claims?

32. Whose victory was announced just two hours after polls closed on June 16?

33. Why did former Ontario attorney-general Michael Bryant spend the night of Sept. 1 in custody?

34. What nickname did many in the media give Falcon Heene?

35. What was the unlikely sentence handed down . to Bernard Madoff on June 29?

36. As what was the CARS program popularly known?

37. Twenty-six gallons is not a lot of water. Why were scientists excited?

38. Which boxer went down for the final count on July 11?

39. Which movie broke a midnight-screening record on Nov. 20?

40. Why was 13 a lucky number for Montreal in 2009?

---

1.July 8 would have been the opening of Michael Jackson’s This Is It tour, the title suggesting the live concerts would be not only his first in years but his last ever. As it happened, the entertainer died of a heart attack in his Los Angeles mansion on June 25. Jackson’s personal physician, Conrad Murray, admitted to administering heavy sedatives. Manslaughter? L.A. police have investigated but laid no charges.

sss

2.Wife of former Liberal leader Stéphane Dion, Krieber attacked his successor, Michael Ignatieff, on her Facebook page and predicted further hard times for the party under his leadership. “For having refused the historic coalition that could have placed it at the head of the left,” Krieber claimed, “it will be punished by history.” She was referring to her husband’s abortive 2008 attempt to defeat the minority Conservative government.

sss

3.Released on Feb. 12, UR was – and still is – available only as a download for the Amazon Kindle reading device. Since the plot concerns an English teacher who himself buys a Kindle, the “book” was viewed by some as an infomercial for the gadget. The Kindle arrived in Canada in November. Was it under the tree?

sss

4. Bertram Earl Jones is the full name of the accused West Island ponzi schemer Earl Jones. The initial news reports of July 11 used the triple-barrelled formula.

sss

5. Stewart Cink won the British Open in July but much attention was focused on his fellow American, 59-year-old Tom Watson, who forced a four-hole playoff. Watson, who was working on a replaced hip, had won the Open on the same Scottish course in 1977.

sss

6. Iceland’s economy crashed in 2008 and Geir (Icelanders use given names) took much of the heat. His resignation as chairman of the Independence party also mentioned his diagnosis with a tumour.

sss

7. The former Vision Montréal leader and lieutenant to mayoral candidate Louise Harel invoked the image of the Mafia in a going-down-swinging interview on Radio-Canada. “Is there a Mafia system that controls city hall?” the confessed money-taker asked himself. “The response is yes.”

sss

8. Chicago, Madrid and Tokyo lost to Rio de Janeiro as the site of the 2016 Summer Olympic Games. The Brazilian city will be the first in South America to play host to an Olympiad. Chicago lost despite the high-profile support of Barack Obama.

sss

9. The Montreal Symphony Orchestra (established 1934) linked itself conceptually to the Montreal Canadiens (established 1909) in a joint sound-and-light birthday celebration in the Bell Centre. Kent Nagano led the orchestra. The hockey team was in Long Island, but many sweater-clad veterans showed up.

sss

10. A “double bird strike” less than a minute after takeoff from New York’s LaGuardia Airport landed a US Airways flight in the Hudson River. Pilot Chesley B. “Sully” Sullenberger III got credit for saving all 155 people aboard, some of whom had to be rescued by police divers. American civil aircraft are estimated to have experienced about 65,000 bird strikes between 1990 and 2005.

sss

11.Son of the head of Paramount Pictures, Schulberg wrote On the Waterfront, a film directed by his fellow friendly witness to the House Un-American Activities Committee, Elia Kazan. Washed-up boxer Terry Malloy (Marlon Brando) lamented how he “coulda been a contender” in the working-class classic.

sss

12. Oops. The Nivose was a French naval patrol boat, not the commercial ship the 11 Somali smalltimers took it to be. The three pirate craft (two for attack, one for supplies) were promptly seized, along with the hapless crew.

sss

13. Oops. Liberal leader Michael Ignatieff thought it was time for a non-confidence vote against the Tories and Stephen Harper. The NDP under Jack Layton had different ideas and abstained. “Mr. Harper, your time is up,” will likely live in political memory for many years.

sss

14. The 67-year-old Nobel Peace Prize winner contracted the H1N1 influenza virus and emerged unscathed. Arias had made medical news the previous year when cysts on his vocal cords led his physicians to prescribe a tough measure for a pol: no talking for a month.

sss

15. Italian Prime Minister Silvio Berlusconi, also in the news for his partying habits, moved the summit from Sardinia to L’Aquila after an earthquake rocked the town, the capital of Abruzzo. The April 6 earthquake killed 286 and damaged historical buildings. Leaders, including Stephen Harper, got tours of the devastated city.

sss

16. “Yankee Stadium” now refers not to the 1923 House that Ruth Built but a snazzy $1.5 billion park nearby. Many of the stratospherically-priced best seats remained empty – not a good look on television.

sss

17.So said U.S. President Barack Obama in Stockholm on Dec. 10 as he accepted his early-bird-special Nobel Peace Prize. “... I am at the beginning, and not the end, of my labours on the world stage,” he continued by way of explaining his reservations.

sss

18. What the U.S. Geological Survey detected as a 4.7-magnitude earthquake at around 10 a.m. Eastern Time was described by the North Korean government itself as a nuclear test about an hour later. Missile firings by the rogue nation followed, just in case we did not get the point. The macho display was probably meant to counter any notion that the likely retirement of ailing dictator Kim Jong-il would produce a less bellicose foreign policy.

sss

19. On June 28 about 100 soldiers stormed the presidential residence in the little-known capital of Honduras and flew its occupant, Manuel Zelaya, to Costa Rica. Zelaya had been trying, against the decision of the Supreme Court, to eliminate constitutionally entrenched presidential term limits. Pronounce Tegucigalpa “te-goo-see-GAL-pa.”

sss

20. The solar eclipse of July 22 could been seen through wide areas of China, India, Japan and southeast Asia. To say it drew a crowd is putting it mildly. The totality duration of 6 minutes 39 seconds (not extraordinary in its own right) will not be exceeded until 2132.

sss

21.The terrorist convicted of 270 counts of murder for the 1988 bombing of Pan Am Flight 103 was released from detention in Scotland because he was suffering from prostate cancer. Many were shocked by the “compassionate” action of the Scottish government. Megrahi got a hero’s welcome and is now living in his family villa.

sss

22. The quick answer is Europe; European Union is more precise; European Council is more precise still. The 62-year-old Belgian prime minister was thought by many to be a bland choice for the first president of a united Europe. Why not Tony Blair?

sss

23. Barack Obama lost no time after his inauguration in ordering the closing of the Guantanamo Bay detainment facility in Cuba. On Dec. 15 the U.S. president named the Thomson Correctional Centre, in Thomson, Illinois as the new home of the 210 remaining Gitmo prisoners. Congressional approval and structural modifications of the prison are still months away.

sss

24. Meeting in Fredericton, Jean Charest of Quebec and Shawn Graham, his counterpart in New Brunswick, agreed to the sale of NB Power to Hydro-Québec for $4.8 billion, a sum that would retire the eastern utility’s debt. Assurances of rate freezes did not completely quell worries in the maritime province.

sss

25. Claude Lévi-Strauss asserted the similarity of human cultures everywhere and bolstered the anthropology of the still-trendy philosophy of structuralism. He is not to be confused with the American jeans manufacturer.

sss

26. “After much prayer and months of careful thought,” Oprah Winfrey announced that her Chicago-based show would end in Sept. 2011. This was one of the great non-stories of the year: The interview queen is expected simply to revive the show on OWN -- the Oprah Winfrey Network.

sss

27. Former Outremont MP Martin Cauchon wanted to make a comeback, against the wishes of Quebec Liberal Party lieutenant Denis Coderre, who had earmarked the plum riding for businesswoman Nathalie Le Prohon. (She later withdrew.) Overruled by Michael Ignatieff and (allegedly) the Toronto-based organizers of the party, Coderre resigned. Much punditry ensued.

sss

28. Cellist Yo-Yo Ma ended up playing backup to Stephen Harper in the NACO gala. The PM waged battle against his anti-arts image by sitting at the piano and singing With A Little Help From My Friends.

sss

29. Slumping economy notwithstanding, the $11-billion CityCentre hotel, casino and shopping complex opened in the heart of Las Vegas Blvd., or the Strip, as it is popularly known. Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design (LEED) certification is promised in a city not know for green consciousness.

sss

30. Subject of a scandal himself, the Late Show host was making light of the Gillette decision to drop its advertisements featuring Tiger Woods. The Proctor & Gamble company said it wanted to “support his desire for privacy.”

sss

31. On Feb. 12 three judges hearing separate cases found that the combined MMR vaccination against measles, mumps and rubella could not be linked to autism. The families were seeking compensation from a federal vaccine-injury fund. Suspicions about the supposed side effects of shots – including the H1N1 flu vaccine – appear to be ineradicable.

sss

32. Electoral authorities in Iran wasted no time in announcing the re-election of President Mahmoud Ahmadinejad by a surprising margin of 63 per cent. Nor did they waste much effort in counting the paper ballots, in the view of the young Iranians who supported runner-up Mir Hussein Moussavi. Demonstrations were of no avail.

sss

33. Bryant got involved in an onroad argument that ended in the death of bicycle courier Darcy Allen Shepherd. Was Shepherd intoxicated? Did he seize the steering wheel of Bryant’s Saab? All this will surely be aired in the trial expected in January.

sss

34. Six-year-old Falcon Heene became Balloon Boy after world media followed his supposed Oct. 15 voyage in Colorado aboard a home-made Helium balloon. In fact he was hiding in the Heene family home. “...We did this for the show,” the young non-pilot said in a television interview, referring to his publicity-obsessed parents.

sss

35. U.S. District Judge Denny Chin gave the 71-year-old Ponzi schemer the theoretical maximum of 150 years, a sentence with no parole. “Symbolism is important,” Judge Chin explained.

sss

36. Car Allowance Rebate System is clear enough but Cash for Clunkers flowed more readily off the tongue. The $1-billion program ran out of cash (but not clunkers) just days after transactions started on July 24. An extra $2 billion extended the program through most of August.

sss

37. The water was found in a permanently shadowed crater near the south pole of the moon. The upper stage of NASA’s Lunar Crater Observation and Sensing Satellite (LCROSS) obligingly crashed while the rest of the spacecraft collected post-traumatic data from the plume of ejecta. Water on the moon means that it might be possible to start a colony there. Now all we need is a reason to go.

sss

38. Italian-born, Montreal-trained Arturo Gatti, renowned for his all-out style, was found dead on July 11 in a hotel room in a coastal Brazilian city where the retired boxer was planning to attend his sister’s wedding, Did Amanda Rodrigues, his ex-stripper wife, strangle him (as Brazilian authorities initially suspected) or did he hang himself (as they later concluded)?

sss

39. What better time than midnight to see The Twilight Saga: New Moon, a vampire movie based on Stephenie Meyer’s wildly successful vampire romances for young adults? The early start helped propel the film to a record single-day domestic gross of $72.7 million.

sss

40. This was how many Saskatchewan Roughriders were on the field for an unsuccessful Montreal Alouettes field goal attempt in the dying seconds of the Grey Cup game in Calgary. The ensuing penalty gave placekicker Damon Duval his second chance, which he nailed, and pushing the Als ahead of their stunned opponents, 28-27.
